The Paradox of Kasb and Faith in Mu'tazilite Thought
Author highlights a paradox in Mu'tazilite view on creation of faith and acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the Mu'tazilite view on acquisition (kasb) and faith, as presented by the author.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilite logic leads to a paradox: created faith without acquisition makes the servant a believer, but with acquisition, God is the believer.

The author presents a curious case: if God creates faith in a servant as an acquisition (kasb) with the servant's choice, the servant would not be a believer—God would. But if God creates faith without any acquisition, the servant would be a believer. This reverses the expected roles.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the concept of kasb
Kasb (acquisition) is the Ash'ari concept that humans acquire actions God creates. The Mu'tazilites reject this, but the author uses it hypothetically.
The argument is based on their own denial of God creating actions.
2
Read the passage on the paradox
Focus on the sentence starting with 'ومن العجب العجيب' which presents the two scenarios.
The author points out the inconsistency.
3
Analyze the two scenarios
First scenario: God creates faith as a kasb with the servant's choice and power — according to Mu'tazilite thought, God would be the believer. Second scenario: God creates faith without any acquisition or power — the servant would be the believer.
This is opposite to what Mu'tazilites would expect.
4
Reflect on the sarcastic conclusion
The author ends by mocking the Mu'tazilites, suggesting that even if they were partners in divinity, they should be ashamed of such reasoning.
The absurdity is highlighted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عنه أن نقول: أي شيء تعنون بمشيئة القصر والجبر؟ فتفرقوا عند ذلك في تفسيرها، فزعم أبو الهذيل ومن تابعه أن تفسير ذلك بأن يخلق فيهم الإيمان جبراً بدون اختيارهم فيوجد فيهم الإيمان ويندفع الكفر. قيل لهم: إن من مذهبكم أن المؤمن هو فاعل الإيمان والكافر هو فاعل الكفر، ولهذا أبيتم أن يكون الله تعالى خالقاً لأفعال الخلق لأنه لو كان خالقاً لكان هو المؤمن الكافر المطيع العاصي المصلي الصائم، فعلى هذا لو خلق فيهم الإيمان لكان هو المؤمن لا العباد فلا يتصور إيمانهم ولم تنفذ مشيئة فبطل قوله: {فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ} وقوله: {وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا} إذ له قدرة جعل نفسه مؤمناً لا قدرة جعل الكافر مؤمناً، وكذا ما اندفع عنه العجز عن جعل الكافر مؤمناً بل له القدرة على جعل نفسه مؤمناً فلو شاء لأمن بنفسه وأتى نفسه هداها لا غير. ومن العجب العجيب أنه لو خلق في العبد إيماناً كسباً له باختياره وتعلقت قدرته به لم يكن العبد مؤمناً بل كان الله تعالى به مؤمناً، لأنه هو الذي أوجد الإيمان، ولو خلق فيه إيماناً وهدى بلا اختيار من جهة العبد ولا اكتساب ولا تعلق قدرته به لكان العبد مؤمناً. ولو كان الله تعالى أشرك المعتزلة في ربوبيته وفوض إليهم نصب أدلة دينه وعلق ذلك باختيارهم فأوجب على جميع الأمم الانقياد إليهم والرضا لصنيعهم والقبول لتحكمهم لكان الأولى بهم أن يستحيوا عن مثل هذا الكلام ونصب مثل هذا الدليل، فكيف ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك.
And the answer to it is that we say: What do you mean by 'the will of restriction and compulsion'? So they differed in its interpretation. Abu Hudhayl and his followers claimed that its interpretation is that He creates faith in them by compulsion without their choice, so faith comes to exist in them and disbelief is repelled. It was said to them: It is part of your doctrine that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and for this reason you refused that Allah Most High is the creator of the actions of creatures, because if He were the creator, He would be the believer, the disbeliever, the obedient, the disobedient, the prayer-performing, the fasting-performing. So on this, if He created faith in them, He would be the believer, not the servants, so their faith would not be conceivable, and the will would not be executed. Thus His statement is invalidated: {For if He willed, He would have guided you all} and His statement: {And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance} because He has the power to make Himself a believer, not the power to make the disbeliever a believer. Similarly, incapacity to make the disbeliever a believer is not repelled from Him, but rather He has power to make Himself a believer; so if He willed, He would believe by Himself and give His own soul its guidance, no other. And from the strangest of wonders is that if He created in the servant faith as an acquisition for him by his choice and his power was attached to it, the servant would not be a believer, but rather Allah Most High would be a believer through it, because He is the one who brought faith into existence; and if He created in him faith and guidance without choice on the servant's part, nor acquisition, nor attachment of his power to it, the servant would be a believer. And if Allah Most High had made the Mu'tazila partners in His lordship and delegated to them the establishment of the proofs of His religion and attached that to their choice, and then obligated all nations to submit to them, be pleased with their actions, and accept their arbitrary judgments, it would be more fitting for them to be ashamed of such speech and the establishment of such a proof. But how could that be, when none of that has occurred?
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation of divine will as compulsion (mashi'ah al-qasr wa al-jabr). The author begins by asking what they mean by this term, noting that they differ in its explanation. Abu Hudhayl and his followers interpret it as God creating faith in people by force without their choice, resulting in faith and removal of disbelief. The author then objects using the Mu'tazilites' own principles: they hold that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and they deny that God creates human actions because that would make God the agent—making Him the believer, disbeliever, etc. The author argues that if God created faith by force, He would be the believer, not the servants, so their faith would not occur and God's will would not be fulfilled. This invalidates verses like 'If He willed, He would have guided you all' because God only has power to make Himself a believer, not to make a disbeliever a believer. The author then highlights a strange inconsistency: if God created faith in a servant as an acquisition (kasb) with the servant's choice and power, the servant would not be a believer according to their logic—God would be the believer. Yet if God created faith without any acquisition or power from the servant, the servant would be a believer. This inverts their expected outcome. Finally, the author sarcastically suggests that if the Mu'tazila were partners with God in lordship, they should be ashamed of such reasoning, but in reality they are not.

Key Terms
كسب
المؤمن فاعل الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mu'tazilites think their view on human agency is consistent; the author shows it leads to a contradiction regarding who is the believer.
Correction: The paradox shows that according to their own principles, a person would be considered a believer only when they have no role in acquiring faith.

Checkpoint
According to the author, in which scenario does the servant become a believer, according to Mu'tazilite logic?
A) When God creates faith in him as an acquisition with his choice.
B) When God creates faith in him without any choice or acquisition.
C) When he acquires faith by his own power.
D) When God delegates authority to Mu'tazilites.

Key Takeaway
The author exposes a logical paradox in Mu'tazilite thought: according to their principles, created faith with acquisition makes God the believer, while created faith without acquisition makes the servant a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt proud of your faith as if it were your own achievement? How does the author's paradox challenge that feeling, and what does it demand of your relationship with Allah?
?
If faith is ultimately a gift from God, even when you think you are 'acquiring' it through effort, what does that mean for your sense of spiritual responsibility? Can you pinpoint a time you acted as if your iman were self-made?
?
The author suggests that attributing faith to yourself leads to a logical absurdity. Does that hit home? Are you willing to admit that even your best choices are not the true origin of your belief, and what would change in your life if you fully accepted that?

Knowledge and Faith are Distinct
Author presents al-Jubba'i's claim and refutes it by distinguishing knowledge from faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi author refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that God creates necessary knowledge that leads to faith, based on the principle that knowledge and faith are distinct.

Core Idea
Knowledge of faith is not faith itself; one can exist without the other.

Al-Jubba'i attempted to salvage the Mu'tazilite position by claiming that God's will of compulsion means He creates necessary knowledge in the servant, which then leads inevitably to faith. The author declares this corrupt because knowledge of faith is distinct from faith itself. In this lesson, we examine the author's core argument that the existence of one does not necessitate the other, and why this refutes al-Jubba'i.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Jubba'i's claim
Read the first sentence where al-Jubba'i defines mashi'at al-jabr as God creating necessary knowledge and proofs so that they believe.
Notice the claim is about necessary knowledge (al-'ilm al-daruri).
2
Understand the author's refutation
Read the author's immediate response: 'This is corrupt because...' (wa hadha fāsid).
The author states the reason clearly.
3
Grasp the distinction
Focus on the sentence: knowledge of faith is other than faith itself, and one does not necessitate the other.
This is the logical core of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما رأى الجبائي عوار هذا الكلام وتشنيع أهل الحق عليهم زعم أن تفسير مشيئة الجبر أن يخلق الله تعالى في العبد العلم الضروري بصحة الإسلام وحقيقته ويقيم له الدلائل المثبتة له العلم الضروري بذلك فيؤمنوا حينئذ. وهذا فاسد لأن العلم بصحة الإيمان وحقيقة الدين غير الدين والإيمان، وليس من ضرورة وجود أحد المتغايرين وجود الآخر لا محالة، بل من الجائز أنه لا يوجد. ألا ترى أن الله تعالى قال: {وَلَوْ أَنَّنَا نَزَّلْنَا إِلَيْهِمُ الْمَلَائِكَةَ وَكَلَّمَهُمُ الْمَوْتَى وَحَشَرْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ قُبُلًا مَّا كَانُوا لِيُؤْمِنُوا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ} أخبر أنه وإن أقام كل دليل لا يؤمنون إلا أن يشاء الله تعالى إيمانهم، فكان في الآية وجهان ينبئان عن بطلان هذا الكلام: أحدهما أن قيام هذه الدلائل غير ومشيئة الإيمان غير حيث قال عز وجل: {مَّا كَانُوا لِيُؤْمِنُوا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ} بعد وجود هذه الدلائل. والآخر: أنه تعالى أثبت أن بقيام هذه الدلائل لا يؤمنون فثبت أن ليس من ضرورة ثبوت الدليل أو العلم به ثبوت الإيمان. وكذا قال: {وَإِن يَرَوْا كُلَّ آيَةٍ لَا يُؤْمِنُوا بِهَا} فمن قال يؤمنون بها محالة فقد كذب الله تعالى في خبره. وقال تعالى: {وَإِن يَرَوْا كِسْفًا مِّنَ السَّمَاءِ سَاقِطًا يَقُولُوا سَحَابٌ مَرْكُومٌ}. ويحققه أن أهل العناد لم يكونوا يؤمنون وإن كان العلم بطريق الحقيقة ثابتاً لهم كما قال تعالى: {يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ وَإِنَّ فَرِيقًا مِّنْهُمْ لَيَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ}. فثبت أن وجود الإيمان والهداية ليس من ضرورة العلم والدليل.
When al-Jubba'i saw the flaw in this speech and the rebuke of the people of truth against them, he claimed that the interpretation of 'the will of compulsion' is that Allah Most High creates in the servant necessary knowledge of the soundness of Islam and its truth, and establishes for him proofs that affirm necessary knowledge of that, so that they would then believe. And this is corrupt because knowledge of the soundness of faith and the truth of religion is other than religion and faith, and it is not necessarily entailed that the existence of one of two distinct things requires the existence of the other inevitably; rather, it is possible that it does not exist. Do you not see that Allah Most High said: {And even if We sent down to them the angels and the dead spoke to them and We gathered before them every thing directly, they would not believe unless Allah wills}? He informed that even if He establishes every proof, they will not believe unless Allah Most High wills their faith. So in the verse there are two aspects that indicate the corruption of this speech: One is that the establishment of these proofs is other than the willing of faith, where He said, Mighty and Majestic: {They would not believe unless Allah wills} after the existence of these proofs. The other is that He, Exalted, confirmed that with the existence of these proofs they do not believe, so it is established that it is not necessary that the existence of the proof or knowledge of it entails the existence of faith. Likewise He said: {And even if they see every sign, they would not believe in it}. So whoever says they would inevitably believe has lied against Allah Most High in His report. And He said, Exalted: {And if they see a fragment from the sky falling, they say: 'Piled-up clouds.'} And what confirms it is that the people of obstinacy would not believe even if knowledge of the truth were established for them, as He said, Exalted: {They recognize it as they recognize their own sons, and indeed a party of them conceal the truth while they know}. So it is established that the existence of faith and guidance is not necessarily consequent upon knowledge and proof.
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'the will of compulsion' (mashi'at al-jabr). Al-Jubba'i, seeing the weakness of Abu Hudhayl's position, claimed that God creates necessary knowledge in the servant about the truth of Islam and establishes proofs, so that they would then believe. The author declares this corrupt and proceeds to prove his point. The core argument is that knowledge of the truth of faith is distinct from faith itself. The existence of one does not necessitate the existence of the other; it is possible for knowledge to exist without faith. The author then cites Quranic evidence: verse 6:111 states that even if angels were sent down and the dead spoke, they would not believe unless Allah wills. This verse contains two points: first, the establishment of proofs is different from the willing of faith, as the verse says they would not believe 'unless Allah wills' after the proofs; second, the verse affirms that with proofs they do not believe, proving that faith does not necessarily follow from proof or knowledge. Additional verses (6:25, 52:44, 2:146) are cited to show that obstinate people see signs and have knowledge but still disbelieve. Thus, faith and guidance are not necessary consequences of knowledge and proof. This refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that creating necessary knowledge would necessarily lead to faith.

Key Terms
الجبائي
مشيئة الجبر
العلم الضروري
تغاير العلم والإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that if God grants someone necessary knowledge of the truth of Islam, that person will inevitably have faith.
Correction: Knowledge and faith are distinct. One can have knowledge of the truth and still not believe, as the author argues and will later prove with Quranic verses.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is al-Jubba'i's interpretation corrupt?
A) Because knowledge of faith is distinct from faith itself, so one does not necessitate the other.
B) Because God does not actually create necessary knowledge.
C) Because faith can never be achieved through knowledge.
D) Because al-Jubba'i misinterpreted the will of compulsion.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of faith is not identical to faith, so its existence does not guarantee belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have clear knowledge of a truth about Allah, do you always act on it? What prevents you from turning that knowledge into faith? Reflect on an area where you know but do not believe enough to change.
?
This lesson proves that knowledge alone does not compel faith. In your own life, where have you relied on intellectual understanding without genuine surrender? Will you ask Allah for tawfīq to transform your knowledge into true iman?
?
Al-Jubba'i thought that if God gives necessary knowledge, people would be forced to believe. Yet the author argues they remain distinct. Have you ever experienced a moment where you knew something was true but did not submit? What does that say about the relationship between your intellect and your heart? Today, commit to seeking faith that moves beyond mere knowledge.

Quranic Evidence: Knowledge Does Not Necessitate Faith
Author cites Quranic verses to prove that knowledge does not entail faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quranic verses to prove that knowledge and proofs do not necessarily lead to faith, and that faith depends solely on Allah's will.

Core Idea
Even the greatest proofs do not compel belief; faith is from Allah's will alone.

After establishing that knowledge and faith are distinct, the author now turns to the Quran to demonstrate that knowledge and proofs do not necessitate faith. Verse 6:111 is central, showing that even if all proofs are given, people would not believe unless Allah wills. This lesson explores the two aspects of that verse and additional evidence from other verses.

Guided Path
1
Read verse 6:111 and its two implications
Read the citation of verse 6:111 and the author's extraction of two points: first, the proofs are distinct from Allah's willing of faith; second, the verse proves that with proofs they do not believe.
These two aspects are the backbone of the argument.
2
Examine additional verses
Read the subsequent verses cited (6:25, 52:44, 2:146) which show that people can have knowledge or see signs yet still disbelieve.
These verses reinforce the point that knowledge does not necessitate faith.
3
Conclude the argument
Read the final sentence where the author concludes that faith and guidance are not necessarily consequent upon knowledge and proof.
This is the summary of the entire refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

When al-Jubba'i saw the flaw in this speech and the rebuke of the people of truth against them, he claimed that the interpretation of 'the will of compulsion' is that Allah Most High creates in the servant necessary knowledge of the soundness of Islam and its truth, and establishes for him proofs that affirm necessary knowledge of that, so that they would then believe. And this is corrupt because knowledge of the soundness of faith and the truth of religion is other than religion and faith, and it is not necessarily entailed that the existence of one of two distinct things requires the existence of the other inevitably; rather, it is possible that it does not exist. Do you not see that Allah Most High said: {And even if We sent down to them the angels and the dead spoke to them and We gathered before them every thing directly, they would not believe unless Allah wills}? He informed that even if He establishes every proof, they will not believe unless Allah Most High wills their faith. So in the verse there are two aspects that indicate the corruption of this speech: One is that the establishment of these proofs is other than the willing of faith, where He said, Mighty and Majestic: {They would not believe unless Allah wills} after the existence of these proofs. The other is that He, Exalted, confirmed that with the existence of these proofs they do not believe, so it is established that it is not necessary that the existence of the proof or knowledge of it entails the existence of faith. Likewise He said: {And even if they see every sign, they would not believe in it}. So whoever says they would inevitably believe has lied against Allah Most High in His report. And He said, Exalted: {And if they see a fragment from the sky falling, they say: 'Piled-up clouds.'} And what confirms it is that the people of obstinacy would not believe even if knowledge of the truth were established for them, as He said, Exalted: {They recognize it as they recognize their own sons, and indeed a party of them conceal the truth while they know}. So it is established that the existence of faith and guidance is not necessarily consequent upon knowledge and proof.
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Jubba'i's interpretation of 'the will of compulsion' (mashi'at al-jabr). Al-Jubba'i, seeing the weakness of Abu Hudhayl's position, claimed that God creates necessary knowledge in the servant about the truth of Islam and establishes proofs, so that they would then believe. The author declares this corrupt and proceeds to prove his point. The core argument is that knowledge of the truth of faith is distinct from faith itself. The existence of one does not necessitate the existence of the other; it is possible for knowledge to exist without faith. The author then cites Quranic evidence: verse 6:111 states that even if angels were sent down and the dead spoke, they would not believe unless Allah wills. This verse contains two points: first, the establishment of proofs is different from the willing of faith, as the verse says they would not believe 'unless Allah wills' after the proofs; second, the verse affirms that with proofs they do not believe, proving that faith does not necessarily follow from proof or knowledge. Additional verses (6:25, 52:44, 2:146) are cited to show that obstinate people see signs and have knowledge but still disbelieve. Thus, faith and guidance are not necessary consequences of knowledge and proof. This refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that creating necessary knowledge would necessarily lead to faith.

Key Terms
آية الأنعام 111
آية الأنعام 25
آية الطور 44
آية البقرة 146

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of verse 6:111 as cited by the author?
A) It shows that proofs necessarily lead to faith.
B) It shows that people will not believe unless Allah wills, even with proofs.
C) It shows that angels can cause belief.
D) It shows that faith is automatic.

Key Takeaway
Quranic evidence confirms that even with full knowledge, faith is not compelled; it depends on divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which sign of Allah – in creation, in your life, or in the Quran – have you seen clearly yet not submitted to fully? What is holding you back, and what would it mean for you to honestly confess that your faith depends not on proofs but on Allah's will?
?
You know that you will die and stand before Allah. You know the Quran is true. Yet what area of your life still operates as if you need more evidence before you obey? If knowledge alone doesn't force faith, then what is your excuse for delaying repentance?
?
The people described in this lesson recognized the truth like they recognize their own children – yet they concealed it. Is there a truth about yourself, your sins, or your relationship with Allah that you are concealing even from yourself? What would it cost you to stop hiding and believe fully?

Refutation of Mu'tazila on Divine Will: The Case of 'If Allah Wills'
Refutation of Mu'tazila by showing their view implies calling Prophet and Ummah liars, and conflicts with fiqh and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila position on divine will leads to absurd consequences, including attributing lying to the Prophet and the Ummah, and how the phrase 'إن شاء الله' (if Allah wills) in oaths and promises refutes their view.

Core Idea
If 'إن شاء الله' doesn't affect obligation, then the Prophet and his Ummah would be liars.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of the Mu'tazila view on divine will. The author shows that if their position were true, it would lead to an inversion of reality, calling the entire Muslim community liars. He then brings a concrete example from fiqh to demonstrate the practical consequences, and finally uses the Quranic command to say 'إن شاء الله' to seal the argument. Let's work through this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Get a sense of the author's flow of argument.
Notice the parentheses in Arabic indicate restored text from footnotes.
2
Identify the inversion and its implication
The author shows that if one applied Mu'tazila principles consistently, the statement 'What God did not will happens and what He willed does not happen' would be more correct, which he calls an 'inversion'. This inversion implies that the Prophet and the Ummah are liars. Ask yourself why that would be.
3
Examine the fiqh example: oaths and promises
The author brings a legal consensus: if someone swears or promises with the condition 'إن شاء الله' and fails, no oath-breaking or blame occurs. This supports the view that God's will is effective. Consider how the Mu'tazila view would change this ruling.
The hadith 'مطل الغنى ظلم' (delay by the wealthy is oppression) shows the gravity of not paying a debt, yet with 'إن شاء الله' there is no blame.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
The author interprets 'إلا أن يشاء الله' as 'except if Allah wills that I not do it.' He argues that on Mu'tazila grounds, this condition would be meaningless because God's will is already determined by the nature of the act (obedience vs disobedience). Why does this refute them?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لم يأتمر أمر الله لم يخرج عما هو حكم أمره وهو الوجوب ولا سبيل لأحد على دفعه فكان نافذا فصدقت الأمة بما قالوا فأما قولهم: (ما شاء الله كان لو كان على ما يقوله المعتزلة لكانت الأمة بأسرهم كاذبين بل لو قيل على أصل المعتزلة ) ( ما لم يشأ الله كان وما شاء لم يكن كان أصوب على أصول المعتزلة وأقرب إلى الصواب إذ ما شاء فلم يكن وما لم يشأ فكان أكثر من القلب، وفيه نسبة النبي عليه السلام أولاً ونسبة جميع أمته ثانيًا إلى الكذب، ومن هذا قوله فلا خفاء بكفره. ومما يحقق ما ذهبنا إليه أن الفقهاء بأسرهم اتفقوا أن من قال لغريمه: والله لأقضي حقك غدا إن شاء الله تعالى ثم لم يقض لم يحنث، ولو وعد فقال: لأقضي غدًا حقك إن شاء الله تعالى ولم يقض لا يلحقه لائمة الخلف، وقضاء الحق المستحق مأمور به والامتناع عنه ظلم على ما روي مطل الغنى ظلم، ولو كان الأمر على ما يقول المعتزلة لحنث الأول وللحق الثاني لأئمة لثبوت مشيئة الله تعالى بذلك وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تَقُولَنَّ لِشَيْءٍ إِنِّي فَاعِلٌ ذَلِكَ غَدًا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ أي إلا أن يشاء الله أن لا أفعل، وعلى زعم المعتزلة لو كان الفعل الموعود طاعة لا يشاء الله أن لا يفعل، ولو كان معصية لا يشاء الله أن يفعل فلم يكن لقوله: إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ فائدة، والله الموفق.
And whoever does not comply with God's command does not depart from what is the ruling of His command, which is obligation. And no one has a way to repel it, so it is effective. So the community affirmed what they said. As for their statement: 'What God wills happens; if it were as the Mu'tazila say, then the entire community would be liars. But if it were said according to the principle of the Mu'tazila: "What God did not will happens, and what He willed does not happen," that would be more correct according to the principles of the Mu'tazila and closer to correctness, since what He willed did not happen and what He did not will happened is more of an inversion. And in this there is attributing lying to the Prophet, peace be upon him, first, and to all his community second. And from this, his statement: there is no concealment of his disbelief. And what confirms what we have gone to is that the jurists in their entirety agreed that whoever says to his creditor: 'By Allah, I will pay your debt tomorrow if Allah wills,' and then does not pay, he does not break his oath. And if he promised and said: 'I will pay your debt tomorrow if Allah wills,' and he did not pay, no blame of breaking a promise attaches to him. Paying the due debt is commanded, and refraining from it is oppression, as it is narrated: 'Delay by the wealthy is oppression.' If the matter were as the Mu'tazila say, the first would break his oath and the second would be blamed for the existence of God's will regarding that. And Allah, exalted, said: 'And never say of anything, "Indeed, I will do that tomorrow," except [when adding], "If Allah wills."' [Quran 18:23-24] i.e., except if Allah wills that I do not do it. And according to the claim of the Mu'tazila, if the promised act were obedience, He does not will that it not be done, and if it were disobedience, He does not will that it be done. So there would be no benefit in His saying 'except if Allah wills.' And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 974

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila position on divine will. The author begins by stating a premise: those who do not obey God's command do not escape its ruling (obligation), and God's command is effective. He then presents the Mu'tazila slogan 'ما شاء الله كان' (what God wills happens) and shows that if one were to follow Mu'tazila principles, the opposite statement ('what God did not will happens and what He willed does not happen') would be more consistent, leading to a complete inversion. This inversion implies calling the Prophet and the entire Muslim community liars. The author then brings a supporting proof from fiqh: jurists agree that if someone makes an oath or promise with the condition 'إن شاء الله' (if Allah wills) and fails to fulfill it, there is no sin or blame. This is because God's will is effective in preventing the action. If the Mu'tazila view were correct—that God's will does not necessarily determine outcomes—then the oath-taker would be liable and the promise-breaker would be blamed. The author cites the Quranic command to say 'إلا أن يشاء الله' and interprets it as 'except if Allah wills that I not do it.' He then argues that on Mu'tazila grounds, this conditional phrase would be meaningless, because if the act is obedience, God wills it to happen, and if it is disobedience, God wills it not to happen, making the condition redundant. Thus the Mu'tazila position is refuted by both legal consensus and scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'إن شاء الله' in oaths and promises has no real effect on whether one is obligated or blamed for non-fulfillment; it is just a verbal formula.
Correction: In reality, saying 'إن شاء الله' connects the action to God's will such that if the action does not occur, there is no sin or blame because God did not will it. This is supported by juristic consensus and the Quran.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would be the consequence if the Mu'tazila principle were true regarding the promise 'إن شاء الله'?
A) The oath-taker would not be blamed.
B) The promise-breaker would be blamed and the oath-taker would break his oath.
C) The Prophet would be praised.
D) The jurists would agree with the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila view on divine will is refuted because it leads to the absurd conclusion that the Prophet and the Ummah are liars, and contradicts both established fiqh and clear Quranic command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'إن شاء الله' in your daily promises or plans, do you truly submit to God's will and accept that He may prevent it, or is it just a habit without real trust? How would your attitude change if you believed God's will is always effective?
?
If you were to consistently apply the Mu'tazila view that God's will does not determine outcomes, would your sense of reliance on God and accountability before Him remain the same? Or would it weaken your trust in His power?
?
The passage warns that denying the effectiveness of 'إن شاء الله' can lead to attributing lying to the Prophet and the Ummah. Examine your own heart: do you ever treat this phrase as empty words, thereby undermining the truthfulness of the Islamic tradition? What will you do to restore sincerity in your statements?

The Dialectical Proof from God's Knowledge and Will
The author forces Mu'tazila to admit that God wills everything as He knows it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dialectical argument used by the Maturidi scholar Abu Hanifa to demonstrate that God's will necessarily corresponds to His knowledge.

Core Idea
God's will must execute His knowledge, or He would will ignorance.

In this passage, the author presents a powerful dialectical argument that forces the Mu'tazila into a logical corner. By starting with an undeniable premise about God's knowledge, he leads them to admit that God wills everything exactly as He knows it will be. This argument not only refutes the Mu'tazila position but also grounds the Maturidi doctrine of divine decree in rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dialectical method
Dialectic (muḥāwarah) uses a series of questions to force an opponent to admit a conclusion. Here, the author questions the Mu'tazila step by step.
Notice how each answer leads to a dilemma.
2
Analyze the first question
The first question asks whether God knows the future eternally as it will be. Denial leads to disbelief; affirmation is the only rational option.
3
Analyze the second question
After affirming knowledge, the next question asks whether God wills to execute His knowledge. If they deny, they imply God wills ignorance—which contradicts His wisdom.
This is the key trap.
4
Draw the conclusion
If they affirm, they admit that God wills everything as He knows it. That is exactly the author's intended point, which he attributes to Abu Hanifa.
This shows the corruption of the Mu'tazila school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسأل المعتزلة فنقول : هل علم الله تعالى ما يكون أبدًا على ما يكون؟ فإن قالوا: لا. كفروا، لأنهم جهلوا ربهم ، وإن قالوا: نعم، قيل لهم شاء أن ينفذ علمه كما علم أو لا؟ فإن قالوا: (لا ، قالوا) بأن الله تعالى شاء أن يكون جاهلاً، ومن شاء ذلك فليس بحكيم. وإن قالوا: نعم، أقروا بأنه شاء أن يكون كل شيء كما علم أن يكون، وهذا الذي أردناه فهذا هو المحكي عن أبي حنيفة، وهو لازم للقول، وهو المعقول القوي في المسألة، وبه يظهر غاية فساد مذهبهم.
We ask the Mu'tazila and say: Did Allah, exalted, know what will be eternally as it will be? If they say: No, they disbelieve because they have been ignorant of their Lord. And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: Did He will to execute His knowledge as He knew or not? If they say: No, they said [that] Allah, exalted, willed to be ignorant, and whoever wills that is not wise. And if they say: Yes, they acknowledge that He willed that everything be as He knew it would be. And that is what we intended. This is what is reported from Abu Hanifa. And it is necessary for the statement, and it is the strong rational argument in the matter, and by it appears the utmost corruption of their school.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical argument (muḥāwarah) against the Mu'tazila. The author poses a series of questions. First question: Does God know everything eternally as it will be? If the Mu'tazila deny this, they are guilty of ignorance about their Lord (kufr). If they affirm, then a second question: Does God will to execute His knowledge as He knows it? If they say no, then they are saying that God willed to be ignorant (because His knowledge would not be actualized), and one who wills ignorance is not wise (ḥakīm). If they say yes, they admit that God wills everything to be exactly as He knows it will be. This admission is exactly what the author (and Abu Hanifa) intended. The author then states that this argument is logically necessary and is a strong rational proof that exposes the corruption of the Mu'tazila school.

Key Terms
علم
مشيئة
حكيم
قول
معقول
فساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God's knowledge of future events does not require His will to bring them about, allowing for human free will independent of divine decree.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that if God knows something will happen, His will must be to bring it about as known; otherwise, He would will ignorance, which is impossible for a wise God.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the Mu'tazila say that God does not will to execute His knowledge as He knows?
A) They affirm God's wisdom.
B) They imply that God willed to be ignorant.
C) They admit that God is all-knowing.
D) They reject the argument.

Key Takeaway
The dialectical argument forces the Mu'tazila to admit that God wills everything exactly as He knows it, establishing the rational foundation for divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that everything that happens in your life—including your mistakes and hardships—happens exactly as God knew and willed? If so, how does that affect your response to trials? If not, what part of the argument do you struggle to accept?
?
The Mu'tazila hesitated to affirm God's will over all events because of moral discomfort. Where in your own heart do you resist submitting to God's decree? What would it take for you to surrender that resistance?
?
If God's knowledge of a sin does not make Him its doer, why do you sometimes act as if His foreknowledge excuses your negligence? How does the logical necessity of His will in this passage increase your sense of personal accountability?

The Khabar Argument: God's Promise to Fill Hell
Dilemmatic argument using God's promise to fill Hell

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi scholar uses God's promise to fill Hell to argue that God wills disbelief for those who disbelieve, and how this rebuts the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
God's own promise proves He wills disbelief for the disbelievers.

This passage deploys a logical dilemma based on a clear Quranic verse. The author forces the Mu'tazila to choose between two unacceptable alternatives, ultimately leading them to admit that God wills the disbelief of the inhabitants of Hell. This is a key proof in the Maturidi defense of predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and initial question
Start by reading the Quranic verse (32:13) where God promises to fill Hell. Then note the first question posed: Does God will that this promise be fulfilled?
The verse is the foundation of the entire argument.
2
Follow the first dilemma
If the Mu'tazila say God does not will the fulfillment, they imply He intended to be a liar, which removes them from Islam. If they say yes, the argument moves to the next step.
This dilemma forces the Mu'tazila to accept that God wills the fulfillment.
3
Analyze the second dilemma
Now the question becomes: Does God will to fulfill His promise while the inhabitants are believers or disbelievers? If believers, then God would be unjust (punishing believers), which is impossible. If disbelievers, then they admit God wills their disbelief, which is the Maturidi position.
This is the core of the argument: it forces the Mu'tazila to concede that God wills disbelief.
4
Note the objection and incomplete ending
The author begins to address an objection about the Prophet desiring faith for disbelievers, but the passage cuts off. The intended reply is that the Prophet's desire does not contradict God's will.
The argument is incomplete, but the main point is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خبر ثم نقول: تقرير هذا أيضا في الخبر فيقال: أليس أن الله تعالى قال: (لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ) فلابد من بلى قيل: هل يشاء أن يتحقق ؟ أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، فقد زعموا أنه أراد أن يكون كاذبًا في مقالته إذ لا خلاف بينهم أن الكذب كما يتحقق في الماضي يتحقق في المستقبل إن كان بين أهل السنة فيه خلاف ومن هذا قوله فهو خالع ربقة الإسلام عن عنقه. وإن قالوا: نعم. قيل أيشاء أن يتحقق خبره وهم مؤمنون أم يشاء أن يتحقق خبره وهم كافرون؟ فإن قالوا يشاء أن يتحقق خبره و هم مؤمنون قيل : لو حقق خبره فيهم وهم مؤمنون، أكان عادلاً أم ظالمًا؟ فلابد من القول بأنه يكون ظالمًا قيل : فإن أراد شيئًا لو كان تحقق لكان ظالمًا فقد أراد ظلمًا وهو باطل. فإن قال شاء أن يحقق خبره فيهم وهم كافرون لأنهم شاء أن يتحقق خبره وهو عادل فقد تركوا مذهبهم وانقادوا للحق. فإن قيل: أليس أن النبي عليه السلام كان مريدًا من الكفرة الذين علم الله أنهم يكفرون ولا يؤمنون - الإيمان فكان رسول الله عليه السلام مريدا)( تجهيل
[Regarding] the transmitted report (khabar): Then we say: A confirmation of this also from the transmitted report. It is said: Is it not that Allah, exalted, said: 'I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together' (Quran 32:13)? So necessarily [the answer is] yes. It is said: Does He will that it be fulfilled or not? If they say: No, then they have claimed that He intended to be a liar in His statement, since there is no disagreement among them that lying is realized in the past just as it is realized in the future – even if there is disagreement among Ahl al-Sunna about it. And from this, his statement: He has loosened the rope of Islam from his neck. And if they say: Yes, it is said: Does He will to fulfill His report while they are believers, or does He will to fulfill His report while they are disbelievers? If they say: He wills to fulfill His report while they are believers, it is said: If He fulfilled His report among them while they were believers, would He be just or unjust? It is necessary to say that He would be unjust. It is said: If He intended something whose realization would make Him unjust, then He intended injustice, and that is false. If they say: He wills to fulfill His report among them while they are disbelievers because He wills to fulfill His report and He is just, then they have abandoned their school and submitted to the truth. If it is said: Is it not that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was desiring from the disbelievers whom God knew that they would disbelieve and not believe – faith? So the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was desiring... ignorance (tajhil)?
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage is a transmitted (khabar) proof. The author begins with the Quranic verse in which God promises to fill Hell with jinn and humans all together. He then poses a dilemma: Does God will that this promise be fulfilled or not? If the Mu'tazila say no, they accuse God of intending to be a liar (since the promise is unfulfilled). The author notes that lying applies to future statements as well, according to the Mu'tazila (though there is disagreement among Ahl al-Sunna). Such a position would remove the person from Islam. If they say yes, then a second dilemma: Does God will to fulfill it while the inhabitants are believers or disbelievers? If they say believers, then God would be unjust (since He punishes believers), and intending injustice is false. If they say disbelievers, then they admit that God wills their disbelief, which is the Maturidi position. The passage then begins to address an objection: the Prophet desired faith for disbelievers whom God knew would not believe. The text cuts off, but the point is that the Prophet's desire does not contradict God's will.

Key Terms
خبر
كذب
ظلم
عادل
كافر
مؤمن
ربقة الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God's promise to punish can be fulfilled while the punished are in a state of belief (i.e., that God punishes believers unjustly).
Correction: The passage shows that if God fulfilled His promise on believers, He would be unjust, which is impossible. Therefore, the only consistent interpretation is that God wills the disbelief of those He punishes.

Checkpoint
If the Mu'tazila say God does not will His promise to fill Hell to be fulfilled, what do they imply about God?
A) He is all-powerful.
B) He intended to be a liar.
C) He is just.
D) He is merciful.

Key Takeaway
God's promise to fill Hell with disbelievers logically implies that He wills their disbelief, a cornerstone of the Maturidi doctrine of predestination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's promise to fill Hell is certain and He wills the disbelief of some, do you ever fear that you might be among those He has willed to disbelieve? How does that fear shape your daily choices and your reliance on His mercy?
?
When you find yourself doubting God's justice in the face of evil, do you realize that your doubt might mirror the Mu'tazila's error? How can this lesson's logic strengthen your trust in His decree even when you do not see the full picture?
?
The Prophet desired faith for all, yet God willed that some disbelieve. Are you content to submit to God's will even when it contradicts your own desires or wishes for others? What would it take for you to fully surrender your own plans to His decree?

intermediate
5 min
Dialectical Proof of God's Will Corresponding to His Knowledge
Nasafi argues dialectically that God wills what He knows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a dialectical question to demonstrate that God wills everything exactly as He knows it, and why this refutes the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
God's will must align with His knowledge, or He would will ignorance.

Nasafi presents a powerful logical argument against the Mu'tazila by asking a series of unavoidable questions. Starting from the premise that God knows all things eternally, he forces the opponent to admit that God also wills things exactly as He knows them. This argument, attributed to Abu Hanifa, reveals the internal contradiction in the Mu'tazilite position.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialectical exchange
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the argument proceeds by asking two successive yes/no questions.
The structure is like a logical trap: if the opponent answers either way, they are forced into a conclusion.
2
Analyze the logical necessity
Consider why the second question (whether God wills to execute His knowledge) is necessary. If God knows but does not will accordingly, His knowledge would be ineffective, implying ignorance.
3
Connect to Maturidi theology
Reflect on how this argument establishes the necessary correspondence between God's attributes of knowledge and will, central to Maturidi thought.
This argument is often used to defend predestination (qadar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نسأل المعتزلة فنقول : هل علم الله تعالى ما يكون أبدًا على ما يكون؟ فإن قالوا: لا. كفروا، لأنهم جهلوا ربهم ، وإن قالوا: نعم، قيل لهم شاء أن ينفذ علمه كما علم أو لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، قالوا بأن الله تعالى شاء أن يكون جاهلاً، ومن شاء ذلك فليس بحكيم. وإن قالوا: نعم، أقروا بأنه شاء أن يكون كل شيء كما علم أن يكون، وهذا الذي أردناه فهذا هو المحكي عن أبي حنيفة، وهو لازم للقول، وهو المعقول القوي في المسألة، وبه يظهر غاية فساد مذهبهم.
We ask the Mu'tazila and say: Did God the Exalted know eternally what will be as it will be? If they say: No, they disbelieve, because they are ignorant of their Lord. And if they say: Yes, it is said to them: Did He will to execute His knowledge as He knew it or not? If they say: No, they say that God the Exalted willed to be ignorant, and whoever wills that is not wise. And if they say: Yes, they affirm that He willed everything to be as He knew it would be, and this is what we intended. This is what is reported from Abu Hanifa, and it is necessary for the statement, and it is the strong rational argument in the issue, and by it the utmost corruption of their doctrine becomes apparent.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical argument against the Mu'tazila concerning the relationship between God's knowledge and His will. The author begins by asking the Mu'tazila whether God eternally knows all that will occur exactly as it will occur. If they deny this, they commit disbelief by being ignorant of God. If they affirm it, the author then asks whether God wills to actualize His knowledge as He knows it or not. If they say He does not will to actualize it, that implies God wills to be ignorant, and one who wills ignorance is not wise. If they say He does will to actualize it, they concede that He wills everything to happen exactly as He knows it. This conclusion is attributed to Abu Hanifa and is presented as rationally necessary. The author declares that this argument exposes the complete corruption of the Mu'tazilite position.

Key Terms
علم الله
مشيئة
المعتزلة
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first question the author asks the Mu'tazila?
A) Does God will evil?
B) Does God know eternally what will be as it will be?
C) Is God wise?
D) Does God create human actions?

Key Takeaway
God's will necessarily corresponds to His knowledge; denying this leads to absurd consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that God knows everything and wills exactly what He knows, does that change how you view the events of your life—even the painful ones? Are you able to accept that your struggles are willed by God as part of His perfect knowledge, or do you resist this idea? What would it mean for your trust in God if you denied this correspondence even in your heart?
?
When something happens that you do not understand, do you instinctively question God's wisdom? This argument shows that denying that God wills what He knows leads to absurdity. How can you train yourself to affirm both His knowledge and His will, especially when life feels unfair? What is one concrete step you will take this week to surrender to His decree?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected this correspondence to protect their notion of God's justice. Is there an area in your life where you cling to your own sense of justice over submitting to God's perfect will? What would it cost you to fully embrace that God wills everything exactly as He knows it—even if that includes things you dislike? Are you ready to say, 'I believe and I submit'?

Scriptural Argument from Quran 32:13
Nasafi uses Quranic verse about filling Hell to refute Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses a Quranic verse about filling Hell to force the Mu'tazila to admit that God wills disbelief for some people.

Core Idea
God's promise to fill Hell forces the Mu'tazila to admit He wills disbelief.

Nasafi now turns from logical to scriptural argument, citing Quran 32:13. He poses a series of dialectical questions that corner the Mu'tazila into either accusing God of lying or conceding that God wills disbelief. This passage shows the interplay of divine will, justice, and promise in kalam debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and the literal translation together to get the overall flow of the argument.
Notice the dialectical question-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the initial question
Find where Nasafi asks whether God wills His promise to fill Hell to be fulfilled. This sets up the two main branches.
3
Examine the first branch: 'No'
If the Mu'tazila say God does not will His promise to be realized, they imply He intended to lie. Understand why this is unacceptable.
Nasafi says this removes the 'loop of Islam' from their necks.
4
Examine the second branch: 'Yes'
If they say yes, a second question arises: does He will it while the people are believers or while they are disbelievers? Trace both sub-branches.
5
Conclude the argument
Notice that the only consistent answer is that God wills the promise to be realized while the people are disbelievers. This forces the Mu'tazila to accept that God wills disbelief.
Nasafi concludes they have abandoned their doctrine and submitted to the truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: تقرير هذا أيضا في الخبر فيقال: أليس أن الله تعالى قال: (لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ ) فلابد من بلى قيل: هل يشاء أن يتحقق ؟ أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا، فقد زعموا أنه أراد أن يكون كاذبًا في مقالته إذ لا خلاف بينهم أن الكذب كما يتحقق في الماضي يتحقق في المستقبل إن كان بين أهل السنة فيه خلاف ومن هذا قوله فهو خالع ربقة الإسلام عن عنقه. وإن قالوا: نعم. قيل أيشاء أن يتحقق خبره وهم مؤمنون أم يشاء أن يتحقق خبره وهم كافرون؟ فإن قالوا يشاء أن يتحقق خبره و هم مؤمنون قيل : لو حقق خبره فيهم وهم مؤمنون، أكان عادلاً أم ظالمًا؟ فلابد من القول بأنه يكون ظالمًا قيل : فإن أراد شيئًا لو كان تحقق لكان ظالمًا فقد أراد ظلمًا وهو باطل. فإن قال شاء أن يحقق خبره فيهم وهم كافرون لأنهم شاء أن يتحقق خبره وهو عادل فقد تركوا مذهبهم وانقادوا للحق.
Then we say: The confirmation of this also is in the scriptural report, so it is said: Is it not that God the Exalted said: 'I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together'? So it must be affirmed. It is said: Does He will it to be realized or not? If they say: No, they have claimed that He intended to be a liar in His statement, since there is no disagreement among them that lying, as it occurs in the past, occurs in the future, even if there is disagreement among Ahl al-Sunna about it. And whoever says this has removed the loop of Islam from his neck. And if they say: Yes, it is said: Does He will His report to be realized while they are believers, or does He will His report to be realized while they are disbelievers? If they say: He wills His report to be realized while they are believers, it is said: If He realized His report in them while they were believers, would He be just or unjust? It must be said that He would be unjust. It is said: Then if He intended something which, if realized, would make Him unjust, then He intended injustice, and that is false. If they say: He wills to realize His report in them while they are disbelievers, because He wills His report to be realized and He is just, then they have abandoned their doctrine and submitted to the truth.
Source pages p. 975

Commentary
This passage provides a scriptural proof to support the previous logical argument. The author cites the Quranic verse (32:13) where God declares He will fill Hell with jinn and people. He then poses a series of dialectical questions to the Mu'tazila. First, does God will this promise to be fulfilled? If they say no, that implies God intended to lie, which is disbelief. If they say yes, then does He will it to be fulfilled while those in Hell are believers or while they are disbelievers? If they say while believers, then fulfilling the promise would make God unjust (punishing believers), which is false. If they say while disbelievers, they concede that God wills their disbelief, which aligns with the Sunni position. The author concludes that the Mu'tazila are forced to abandon their doctrine and submit to the truth.

جهنم
الكذب
العدل
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves God directly creates unbelief in people.
Correction: The argument is about God's will to fulfill His promise, not about creating unbelief. The verse is used to force the Mu'tazila to accept that God wills that some people remain disbelievers so that His promise is fulfilled.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi's argument, if the Mu'tazila say God does not will His promise to fill Hell to be realized, what does that imply?
A) God is just.
B) God intended to lie.
C) God is all-powerful.
D) The verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi forces the Mu'tazila to choose between accusing God of lying or conceding that God wills disbelief, thereby defending the Sunni doctrine of divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Mu'tazila tried to protect God's justice by denying His will over disbelief. How does your own heart sometimes resist God's absolute sovereignty? Will you surrender to whatever He wills, even if it seems difficult?
?
This passage forces you to face the reality of Hell as God's certain promise. Have you let this truth shape your urgency for yourself and others? What will you do differently starting today?

Nasafi's Response to the Mu'tazila on Command and Knowledge
Nasafi answers the Mu'tazila argument about commanding disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends the compatibility of God's command with His foreknowledge against a Mu'tazili objection.

Core Idea
God's command does not require His knowledge to change.

The Mu'tazila argued that commanding a disbeliever to believe, while knowing they never will, is either pointless or implies ignorance in God. Nasafi's response uses the very examples of Pharaoh and Abu Jahl to show that the objection collapses under its own logic. In this lesson, we follow the dialectic and see how he turns the argument back on the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage first, then the literal English translation. Notice the structure: an objection (فإن قيل), two possible answers, and a refutation (قلنا).
The passage ends abruptly; the argument is complete enough for our purpose.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The Mu'tazila pose a dilemma: either God did not command Pharaoh and Abu Jahl to believe (making punishment unjust), or He did command them (implying He commands what He knows won't happen, which they deem impossible). Identify both sides.
3
Understand Nasafi's counter-argument
Nasafi responds by pointing out that the Mu'tazila themselves accept that God can command to 'make Himself ignorant' if we follow their logic. He then accuses them of trying to justify the impossible.
Focus on the phrase 'تقرير علمه' – confirming His knowledge.
4
Reflect on the accusation
Nasafi ends by saying the Mu'tazila are ignorant of the realities of meanings (حقيقة المعاني). Consider what this means for theological methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: من علم الله منه أنه لا يؤمن ويموت على الكفر، هل أمره بالإيمان ونهاه عن الكفر أم لا؟ فإن قلتم : لا . فقد زعمتم أن فرعون وأبا جهل ما كانا مأمورين بالإيمان ولا منهيين عن الكفر ، وفيه أنهما ما استحقا اللوم والتعذيب لأنهما ما تركا مأمورًا ولا ارتكبا منهيًا وهو كفر ، وإن قلتم : أمرهما بالإيمان ونهاهما عن الكفر . فقد قلتم : إنه أمرهما بتجهيل نفسه ونهاهما عما فيه تقرير علمه وهذا مما لا خلاف فيه، فإذا جاز بالإجماع أن يأمر بتجهيل نفسه وينهى عما فيه تقرير علمه، ولم يكن ذلك محالاً فلم يجوز أن يريد ما فيه تجهيل نفسه ولا يريد ما فيه تقرير علمه؟ بل يكره ذلك قلنا : أنتم معشر المعتزلة تريدون أبدًا تصحيح المحال بما تصور عندكم من الجائزات أنه يظهر لجهلكم بحقائق المعاني، ولو عقلتم
If it is said: Regarding the one of whom God knows that he will not believe and will die in disbelief, did He command him to believe and forbid him from disbelief or not? If you say: No, then you claim that Pharaoh and Abu Jahl were not commanded to believe nor forbidden from disbelief, and this entails that they did not deserve blame and punishment because they did not abandon a command nor commit a prohibition, which is disbelief. And if you say: He commanded them to believe and forbade them from disbelief, then you say: He commanded them to make Him ignorant and forbade them from what would confirm His knowledge, and this is something about which there is no disagreement. So if it is permissible by consensus for Him to command to make Himself ignorant and forbid what confirms His knowledge, and that is not impossible, then why is it not permissible for Him to will what involves making Himself ignorant and not will what involves confirming His knowledge? Rather, He dislikes that. We say: You, O group of Mu'tazila, always try to correct what is impossible by what you consider to be possibles, because of your ignorance of the realities of meanings. If only you understood...
Source pages p. 976

Commentary
This passage presents a further objection from the Mu'tazila and the author's response. The objection asks whether God commands faith and forbids disbelief to those He knows will not believe (like Pharaoh and Abu Jahl). If the author says no, then these individuals would not deserve punishment, which is absurd. If he says yes, then it implies God commands them to do something that would make Him ignorant (if they actually believed, contrary to His knowledge) and forbids them from something that would confirm His knowledge. The author argues that this is agreed upon as permissible, so why can't God will similarly? The author accuses the Mu'tazila of trying to justify the impossible based on their flawed understanding of what is possible. The passage is cut off but the argument is clear: if commanding such is permissible, then willing similar things is also permissible.

Key Terms

النهي
فرعون
أبو جهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God commands something He knows will not happen, the command is meaningless or implies ignorance.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the command is meaningful because it establishes the basis for accountability, and God's knowledge is not affected by whether the command is obeyed or not.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili dilemma by showing that commanding what one knows will not happen does not contradict God's knowledge or justice; rather, it upholds human accountability.

God's Command Realizes His Foreknowledge
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili objection about God's command to disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that God's command and prohibition are issued to realize His eternal foreknowledge, not to make Him appear ignorant.

Core Idea
God commands the disbeliever to realize His knowledge, not to make him obey.

This passage from Nasafi addresses a key Mu'tazili objection: if God commands a disbeliever whom He knows will disobey, doesn't that make God ignorant? Nasafi turns the objection around, showing that the command is precisely what allows God's foreknowledge to be realized. Without the command, disobedience would not exist, and God's punishment would be unjust.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: Nasafi begins by criticizing the opponent's ignorance, then explains the purpose of command/prohibition, gives the example of Pharaoh, and concludes with a refutation of the Mu'tazili claim.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify key terms
Look for the terms: al-amr wa al-nahy (command and prohibition), al-ilm (knowledge), al-tahqīq (realization), al-tajhīl (making ignorant), and al-Mu'tazila. These are central to the argument.
Understanding these terms will help you follow the logic.
3
Follow the logic of the argument
Trace Nasafi's reasoning: God knows that Pharaoh will disbelieve. Punishment is only for disobedience. Disobedience requires a command. Therefore God commands to make disobedience possible, thus realizing His knowledge. The command is not for obedience but for the realization of God's knowledge.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Contrast with Mu'tazili view
Consider the Mu'tazili claim that if the command aims at obedience, then commanding one who will disobey makes God ignorant. Nasafi says the command aims at disobedience, so it does not make God ignorant. The purpose is tahqīq (realization), not tajhīl.
This refutes the objection.
5
Reflect on the broader principle
Nasafi concludes that all divine commands serve to realize God's knowledge, whether the servant obeys or disobeys. This applies to the believer as well: the command to obey allows obedience to be realized.
This is a key principle in Maturidi thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: هذا كلام تمسكتم به لجهلكم بمذاهب خصومكم ولو عرفتم ذلك حقيقة لما اشتغلتم به، وذلك لأن الأمر والنهي عند خصومكم ورد لتحقيق ما علم الله تعالى وإن كان يتراءى من حيث الظاهر أنهما وردا لمخالفة العلم، وبيان ذلك أنه تعالى علم بسابق علمه أن فرعون يكفر ويعصى ويعاقبه الله تعالى في النار، وكذا غيره من الكفرة وأخبر بذلك ثم لا يعذب إلا على العصيان ولا عصيان بدون الأمر والنهي إذ لو لم يأمر بالإيمان لما وجب تحصيله ولا حرم تركه ولو لم ينه عن الكفر لما حرم تحصيله ولما وجب تركه ولو لم يجب الإيمان ولم يحرم الكفر لكان لا يعاقب الكافر ولا يملأ منه جهنم، فلا يتحقق ما علمه وأخبر به من إدخاله الجنة وإكرامه إياه بالثواب وأمر ونهى من علم منه المعصية لا ليأتمر وينتهي بل ليترك الائتمار والانتهاء فعاقبه الله ويدخله النار، فيتحقق ما علم وما أخبر به، ولولا الأمر والنهي لما تحقق ذلك فكان أمره ونهيه لتحقيق ما علمه وأخبر به، وإنما يكون الأمر على ما زعمت المعتزلة أن لو كان أمر الكافر ليطيعه لا ليعصيه فحينئذ يكون الأمر والنهي لتجهيله وتكذيبه، وأما إذا كان ذلك ليعصي لا ليطيع فكان لتحقيق ما علم وأخبر لا لتجهيله، وصار الحاصل أن من علم الله منه أهل طاعة أمره ليطيع لتتحقق الطاعة إذ لا تحقق لها بدون الأمر، ومن علم منه المعصية أمره لئلا يفعل بل يعصي إذ لا تحقق للمعصية بدون الأمر، وما وقع في أفواه متفقهة زماننا أن فائدة الوجوب بلا داع تلقنوه من المعتزلة فيتكلمون به جهلا منهم بما يؤول إليه من المذهب الباطل، وتقرر بالوقوف على هذه الجملة أن الأمر في الحقيقة لتحقيق ما علم وإن كان يتراءى أنه للتجهيل، والله الموفق.
Then we say: This speech you have clung to is due to your ignorance of the doctrines of your opponents; if you had truly known them, you would not have occupied yourselves with it. That is because, according to your opponents, the command and prohibition are issued to realize what God Almighty has known, even if outwardly they appear to have been issued in opposition to knowledge. The explanation of this is that He Almighty knew by His prior knowledge that Pharaoh would disbelieve and disobey, and He would punish him in the Fire, and likewise other disbelievers, and He informed of that. Then He does not punish except for disobedience, and there is no disobedience without command and prohibition. For if He had not commanded faith, its acquisition would not be obligatory nor its abandonment forbidden; if He had not prohibited disbelief, its acquisition would not be forbidden nor its abandonment obligatory; if faith were not obligatory and disbelief not forbidden, the disbeliever would not be punished and Hell would not be filled with him. Thus what He knew and informed of – of admitting him to Paradise and honoring him with reward – would not be realized. So He commanded and prohibited one whom He knew would disobey, not that he should obey and refrain, but that he should leave off obedience and refrain. Then God punished him and entered him into the Fire, thereby realizing what He knew and informed of. Had there been no command and prohibition, that would not have been realized. Thus His command and prohibition are for the realization of what He knew and informed of. The command would be as the Mu'tazila claim only if He had commanded the disbeliever to obey him, not to disobey him; then the command and prohibition would be for making Him ignorant and lying. But if it is so that he disobeys, not obeys, then it is for the realization of what He knew and informed of, not for making Him ignorant. The upshot is that one whom God knows to be obedient, He commands to obey so that obedience is realized – for there is no realization of it without command; and one whom He knows to be disobedient, He commands so that he does not do it but disobeys, for there is no realization of disobedience without command. What has fallen into the mouths of the pseudo-jurists of our time – that the benefit of obligation is without a motive – they have learned from the Mu'tazila, and they speak out of ignorance of what it leads to of false doctrine. By standing upon this summary it is established that the command in reality is for the realization of what is known, even if it appears that it is for making ignorant. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 977

Commentary
This passage is a response to a Mu'tazili objection about God's command to disbelievers. The author (Nasafi) argues that God's command and prohibition are not for making Him appear ignorant (tajhil), but rather to realize His eternal foreknowledge. The reasoning proceeds as follows: God knows from eternity that certain individuals (like Pharaoh) will disbelieve and be punished. Punishment is only for disobedience, and disobedience is only possible if there is a command. Without a command to believe, faith would not be obligatory; without a prohibition of disbelief, disbelief would not be forbidden. Therefore, if God did not command, His foreknowledge of their punishment would not be realized. Thus He commands the disbeliever not with the intention that he obey, but that he disobey, so that the consequence (punishment) fulfills God's knowledge and announcement. Nasafi contrasts this with the Mu'tazili claim: if the command were intended for obedience, then commanding one who will disobey would make God ignorant. But since the purpose is to realize His knowledge, it is not tajhil. He concludes that the command is always for the realization of what God knows, whether the servant obeys or disobeys, and criticizes those who adopt the Mu'tazili idea that obligation has no purpose (fā'idat al-wujūb bilā dā'ī).

Key Terms
الأمر والنهي
العلم
التحقيق
التجهيل
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God commanding a disbeliever whom He knows will not obey implies God is ignorant or His command is futile.
Correction: Nasafi argues the command is not for obedience but to realize God's foreknowledge of disobedience, thus it does not imply ignorance.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does God command the disbeliever whom He knows will disbelieve?
A) To make them obey
B) To realize His foreknowledge of their disobedience
C) To test them
D) To give them a chance to repent

Key Takeaway
The command and prohibition of God serve to realize His eternal knowledge, not to make Him appear ignorant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a divine command that feels difficult or impossible to obey, do you truly trust that God's command has a purpose even if you fail? How does this lesson embolden you to keep striving, knowing that both obedience and disobedience realize His knowledge? Will you pray for sincerity in obedience while accepting His wisdom over your outcomes?
?
Consider a sin you have committed after knowing it was prohibited. Did you ever think that by sinning you were 'surprising' God or making His command irrelevant? How does the knowledge that God commanded you precisely because He knew you would disobey—yet still holds you accountable—transform your view of repentance and humility before Him? What step will you take today to return to that command with renewed solemnity?
?
This passage argues that God's commands are not for His benefit but for the realization of His eternal knowledge. If you truly internalized that every command you receive is a means for God's knowledge to unfold, would your obedience become more a matter of awe than mere duty? How will you remind yourself of this when you next hear or recite a divine command?

The Objection and Initial Response
Nasafi presents an objection and a brief initial response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection raised against the consistency of God's pleasure and will regarding disbelief and the initial response that dismisses it as analogous to a previous fallacy.

Core Idea
An objection trying to force a contradiction in God's attributes is dismissed as structurally flawed.

Nasafi presents a hypothetical objection from opponents who question how God can approve of faith but not disbelief, given that both occur by His will. The objection tries to argue that God's pleasure would entail ignorance. Nasafi first responds by noting that this is essentially the same as a previous objection about impossible things.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once for the objection and the initial response. Notice how the objection juxtaposes God's pleasure in faith and displeasure in disbelief.
The objection hinges on the idea that if God disapproves of disbelief, then His willing it would be contradictory.
2
Identify the logical structure
The objection has two parts: first, it states the known fact (God does not approve of disbelief), then it asks how He can will it. Identify the assumed contradiction.
3
Understand the initial rebuttal
Nasafi's initial response is that this objection is structurally identical to a previous one about 'rectifying the impossible.' Grasp why he considers it a repetition.
This sets the stage for the more detailed answers that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: أليس أن الله تعالى لا يرضى بالكفر ولا يحبه ويرضى بالإيمان ويحبه، فلما جاز أن يرضى بما لو تحقق لأوجب تجهيله ولا يرضى بما لو تحقق لكان فيه تحقيق علمه؟ فكذا في الإرادة جاز ذلك، قيل: وهذا مثل السؤال الأول أن إرادة تصحيح المحال بما تصور عندكم أنه نظير ذلك المحال. ثم نقول: إن الأشعري يقول : إن الله تعالى يرضى بوجود الكفر من الكافر قبيحا وكذا يجب وجود الكفر قبيحا وقوله تعالى: ( وَلَا يَرْضَى لِعِبَادِهِ الْكُفْرَ ( المراد به المؤمنون دون الكفرة حملت على الخصوص بالدليل فعلى هذا اندفع الإلزام، وعلى قول مشايخنا - رحمهم الله كل واحد منهما أعني الرضا والمحبة لتحقيق ما علم لأن الرضا بالشيء استحسان له وكذا المحبة واستحسان الفعل يخرجه من أن يكون منهيًا، ومن أن يستحق عليه صاحبه العقوبة فلم يستحسن الكفر الذي علم وجوده بل استقبح وكره على ما يقتضى وجوده، إذ هو لن يتصور إلا قبيحا ليكون سببًا للعقوبة وإدخال النار فيتحقق ما علم الله تعالى وما أخبر، والله الموفق.
If they say: Is it not that God Almighty does not approve of disbelief nor love it, and He approves of faith and loves it? So how is it permissible that He approve of that which if realized would necessitate making Him ignorant, and does not approve of that which if realized would contain the realization of His knowledge? So likewise in will, that is permissible. It is said: This is like the first question – the will to rectify the absurd by what you imagine to be similar to that absurd. Then we say: Ash'ari says that God Almighty approves of the existence of disbelief from the disbeliever as ugly, and likewise the existence of disbelief is necessary as ugly. And His statement: "And He does not approve for His servants disbelief" means the believers, not the disbelievers; it is taken as specific by evidence, and thus the objection is repelled. And according to the statement of our masters (may God have mercy on them), each of them, I mean approval and love, is for the realization of what is known, because approval of a thing is considering it good, and likewise love; and considering an action good removes it from being prohibited, and from its doer deserving punishment. So He did not consider disbelief good – which He knew would exist – but rather He considered it bad and hated it in accordance with what its existence requires, for it can only be imagined as ugly in order to be a cause for punishment and entry into the Fire, thereby realizing what God Almighty knew and informed. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 977

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection questions the consistency of God's pleasure: God does not approve of disbelief (according to Quran 39:7), yet He commands it for some? How can He approve of something that would entail making Him ignorant, and not approve of something that realizes His knowledge? The answer first notes that this is similar to the previous objection. Then Nasafi presents two positions: (1) The Ash'ari position: God does approve of the existence of disbelief from the disbeliever as a bad act, and the verse applies only to believers (specific meaning). Thus the objection fails. (2) The Maturidi position (our masters): Both approval (riḍā) and love (maḥabba) are for the realization of divine knowledge. Approval of something means deeming it good. If God deemed disbelief good, it would not be prohibited and would not deserve punishment. Since God knows that disbelief must exist as ugly to be a cause of punishment, He does not deem it good but rather deems it bad and hates it. Thus His disapproval is consistent with His command, as the command is for the realization of His knowledge, not for His pleasure in the act itself.

Key Terms
الرضا
المحبة
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's pleasure and will must always be in agreement, and any divergence implies contradiction.
Correction: The objection assumes a contradiction, but Nasafi shows it is structurally identical to a previously refuted fallacy, implying that the relationship between pleasure and will is more nuanced.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say about the objection in his initial response?
A) It is a new and valid argument
B) It is like the first question about rectifying the absurd
C) It is answered by restricting the verse to believers
D) It is about God's love, not pleasure

Key Takeaway
The objection is dismissed as a rephrasing of an earlier fallacy about divine will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you notice yourself feeling frustrated or confused about why God allows certain things, have you stopped to consider that your objection might be based on a misunderstanding similar to the one dismissed by Nasafi? Will you now actively remind yourself that God's pleasure and will are not in contradiction, and that any apparent conflict stems from your limited understanding?
?
The opponents thought they had discovered a flaw in the doctrine of divine attributes. How often do you assume that modern doubts about God's justice or wisdom are original, when in fact they are recycled fallacies that have been answered by scholars? What practical step will you take to learn from traditional responses before letting such doubts take root in your heart?
?
If you truly believe that God's will and pleasure are perfectly wise, then why do you sometimes feel uneasy when life does not align with your expectations? How will you train your soul to trust in Allah's decree, even when it contradicts your personal desires?
